< Text>
I had my car towed to this Midas location due to the proximity from where my car had stalled out (alternator and battery died). The folks at the counter were helpful, polite and prompt. I received an estimate on the work fairly quickly but it was grossly overpriced at $1,300 versus calling around to other local shops and receiving quotes in the $700-800 range. The dealership quote was even less expensive,   which rarely happens. I called to notify the Midas that I would be having the work done elsewhere. The folks at the counter were also polite and helpful when I came to pick up my car and one of the technicians helped with a battery installation so the vehicle could be driven to the other shop. Overall, I'd say the people were very kind but I can't say anything about the work since I didn't opt to have the vehicle repaired at this location. If you have time, other places will likely be less expensive for the same or similar work.</Text>

< text>
This was the first south Indian food I've tried outside of my partner's parents home. It's definitely not as good as parents home, but it's good.

The first thing I noticed was the beautiful garden and space inside the black gates on sunset blvd. what a contrast once you go in!the waiter even allowed us to safely store our bikes in a corner of the outdoor garden/table area while we ate.

The service was excellent, there was many vegan and vegetarian options, and the dish styles and portions are shareable. South Indian food is mostly water-based and lighter than northern Indian food. I was happy to find a spot that even my partner whose south asian approves. I've gone twice and I'll definitely go again.</text>

< Text>
We visited Paru's on the 29th of December. We were five of us, and quite honestly, our experience wasn't memorable at all. The ambience of the place is really good, with a nice authentic Indian feel to it.. However, we experienced poor service and low food quality. We had to wait quite a while to even get someone to take our order. Additionally, even after we get our Indian thalis, we had to wait quite a while to get a plate of purees and papad we were supposed to get with the food, inspite of reminding them multiple times. Furthermore, the food quality is poor, and the quantity too is very very little, and doesn't justify the price of the food at all. We came with really high hopes, but ended up leaving disappointed.
Definitely worth visiting if you want to get a feel of the Indian vibe in LA, but your taste buds won't be satisfied at all.< /Text>

I went with my family during my visit to LA to this place. The outside appearance of the restaurant was misleading.But once we got in, we found the ambience to be up scale,though too cramped. we ordered for an assorted dinner Ala carte.There was idli,sambar,chutney,rava upma,dosa and vada.i will rate each of the item seperately:
idli- horrible .it was not cooked at all and the shape was bad.did not taste like idli
vada- was hard and oily.probably the batter was old and hence it was hard.
rava upma - was in edible form.better than other items on plate
dosa- again uncooked on one side
chutney- was dead cold.
sambhar - was the saviour of the day. with the help of sambhar i could finish the meal.

well after a very disppointed dinner, we called the manager and gave him the feedback. Guess he was good to us because we too were indians and hence did not charge us the full amount and chopped the bill to 50 %.As a compliment he also gave us a sweet dish and said the cook inside was a mexican and hence he had to be trained more on indian cooking.
He mentioned this place was frequented by americans than indians.Hence he dosent get frequent feedbacks on the quality of food.
verdict- This dosent qualify for the list of good indian restaurants in LA. I still dont know why many reviews say so many good things about this place.This wasnt authentic indian food if you are looking for one.< /Review>

<gmapID>0x80d95723982e9e39:0xe2281cb6d44c0a8b<//gmapID></record></dataset><record>
< review>
Uh, no.‚Å†
‚Å†
Caveat: I generally dislike what some people call taquitos, others call flautas, and what San Diego calls "rolled tacos," which (in San Diego County) are typically cylindrical taco dorados smothered in old guacamole and shredded yellow cheese.
‚Å†
So you can guess how I feel about the much-heralded "Big Rolled Tacos with Shredded Beef" served at Albert's Fresh Mexican Food. I've been told by people who eat this miserable kind of thing that Albert's make the "best" version of this in San Diego, but I just wasn't feelin' it. The shredded beef was dry and tasted like it came out of a tin, the tortilla had the taste of metallic residue, and the guacamole had a pasty texture despite being palatable.‚Å† The frying oil needs to be changed more frequently too, as I'm sure the slightly fishy flavor it imparts is not intentional.

I also tried the (non-big) "Rolled Tacos with Ground Beef," and preferred them slightly, as the meat wasn't as dry and lifeless.
‚Å†
The operation is clean, the people working here are friendly, and the salsa roja is pretty good, which is why Albert's earns three stars, slightly boosted by pandemic sympathy.

Don't worry, Albert's: it's not you, it's me. El Tianguis, La Barbacoa Autentica de Borrego, Tu√©tano Taqueria, and Los Cuatro Milpas make the only rolled tacos/flautas/taquitos in SD that I have deemed fit for human consumption. You're not any worse than all of the rest.‚Å†<//review>

< username>
Ryan Eberle<//username>
< text>
Great park. Large equipmentneith swings and multiple slides. A smaller kid section though it's a little sparse. Lots of concrete picnic benches. Large amount of green space with some medium sized trees. Shade is common but lacking on the equipment. 1 tennis court and 2 basketball courts, and a baseball backstop.

Beautiful park for all sorts of team sports, young kids, and families. Picnics a must.

Biggest downside is lack of a public restroom.</text>
